In <i><a href="/wiki/Just_Shoot_Me!" title="Just Shoot Me!">Just Shoot Me!</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/David_Spade" title="David Spade">David Spade</a>'s character meets up with his childhood male friend, who has transitioned to living as a woman. After initially being frightened, he eventually forms sexual attraction to his friend, but is scorned, as he is 'not her type'. In an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Becker_(TV_series)" title="Becker (TV series)">Becker</a></i> Dr. Becker gets an out-of-town visit from an old friend who turns out to have undergone SRS, it plays out very similar to the situations in <i><a href="/wiki/Just_Shoot_Me!" title="Just Shoot Me!">Just Shoot Me!</a></i>. In a 1980s episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Love_Boat" title="The Love Boat">The Love Boat</a></i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McKenzie_Phillips" title="McKenzie Phillips">McKenzie Phillips</a> portrays a trans woman who is eventually accepted as a friend by her old high school classmate, series regular <a href="/wiki/Fred_Grandy" title="Fred Grandy">Fred Grandy</a>. In the 1970s on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jeffersons" title="The Jeffersons">The Jeffersons</a></i>, George's Navy buddy Eddie shows up as Edie and is eventually accepted by George.</p>
<p>Dramas including <i><a href="/wiki/Law_%26_Order" title="Law &amp; Order">Law &amp; Order</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Nip/Tuck" title="Nip/Tuck">Nip/Tuck</a></i> have had episodes featuring transsexual characters and actresses. While in Nip/Tuck the role was played by a non-transsexual woman, in Law &amp; Order some were played by professional cross-dressers. <i><a href="/wiki/Without_a_Trace" title="Without a Trace">Without a Trace</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_Crime_Scene_Investigation" title="CSI: Crime Scene Investigation">CSI: Crime Scene Investigation</a></i> have had episodes dealing with violence against transsexual characters. Many transsexual actresses and extras appeared on the CSI episode, "Ch-Ch-Changes," including <a href="/wiki/Marci_Bowers" title="Marci Bowers">Marci Bowers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calpernia_Addams" title="Calpernia Addams">Calpernia Addams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The trans woman victim, Wendy, was played by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarah_Buxton_(actress)" title="Sarah Buxton (actress)">Sarah Buxton</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Cisgender" title="Cisgender">cisgender</a> woman. <a href="/wiki/Candis_Cayne" title="Candis Cayne">Candis Cayne</a>, a transsexual actress, appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/CSI:_NY" title="CSI: NY">CSI: NY</a></i> as a transsexual character. From 2007 to 2008, she also portrayed a transsexual character (this time recurring) in the ABC series <i><a href="/wiki/Dirty_Sexy_Money" title="Dirty Sexy Money">Dirty Sexy Money</a></i>.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Hit_%26_Miss" title="Hit &amp; Miss">Hit &amp; Miss</a></i> is a drama about Mia, played by <i><a href="/wiki/Chlo%C3%AB_Sevigny" title="Chloë Sevigny">Chloë Sevigny</a></i>, a preop transsexual woman who works as a contract killer and discovers she fathered a son.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/There%27s_Something_About_Miriam" title="There's Something About Miriam">There's Something About Miriam</a></i> was a 2003 reality television show. It featured six men wooing 21-year-old Mexican model <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miriam_(entertainer)" title="Miriam (entertainer)">Miriam</a> without revealing that she was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-operative_transsexual" title="Pre-operative transsexual">pre-operative</a> <a href="/wiki/Trans_woman" title="Trans woman">trans woman</a> until the final episode.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Coronation_Street" title="Coronation Street">Coronation Street</a>" once had a transsexual woman named Hayley, who was Harold in her childhood. She died on 20 January 2014.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_pageantry">In pageantry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transsexual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: In pageantry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 2004, with the goal of crowning the top transsexual of the world, a beauty pageant by the name of <i><a href="/wiki/The_World%27s_Most_Beautiful_Transsexual_Contest" title="The World's Most Beautiful Transsexual Contest">The World's Most Beautiful Transsexual Contest</a></i> was held in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>. The pageant accepted pre-operation and post-operation trans women, but required proof of their gender at birth. The winner of the 2004 pageant was a woman named <a href="/wiki/Mimi_Marks" title="Mimi Marks">Mimi Marks</a>.</p>
<p>Jenna Talackova, the 23-year-old woman who forced Donald Trump and his Miss Universe Canada pageant to end its ban on transgender contestants, competed in the pageant on May 19, 2012 in Toronto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>On Saturday, January 12, 2013, Kylan Arianna Wenzel was the first transgender woman allowed to compete in a Miss Universe Organization pageant since Donald Trump changed the rules to allow women like Wenzel to enter officially. Miss Wenzel was the first transgender woman to compete in a Miss Universe Organization pageant since officials disqualified 23-year-old Miss Canada Jenna Talackova the previous year after learning she was transgender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events_and_organizations">Events and organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transsexual&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Events and organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transgender#Events" title="Transgender">Transgender § Events</a></div>
<p>Trans communities in various countries hold several events annually; in the United States, the most prominent are the <a href="/wiki/Transgender_Day_of_Remembrance" title="Transgender Day of Remembrance">Transgender Day of Remembrance</a> held every year on November 20, and the <a href="/wiki/Trans_March" title="Trans March">Trans March</a>, one of three protests held in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco, California</a> during "Pride Weekend", the last weekend of June.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/All_About_Trans" title="All About Trans">All About Trans</a> is an organization in the UK whose goal is to influence and improve media professionals' understanding and portrayal of transsexual people. They do this by connecting media outlets with members of the transsexual community throughout the UK in order to foster a greater sensitivity toward this group of people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paris_Lees" title="Paris Lees">Paris Lees</a> works as a facilitator with this organization and was recognized on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Independent_on_Sunday" title="The Independent on Sunday">The Independent on Sunday</a>'s Pink List in 2013 for being the most influential figure in the LGBT community in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Transgender_At_Work&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Transgender At Work (page does not exist)">Transgender At Work</a> (TAW) is an organization with a focus on addressing issues in the workplace for transsexual individuals. Its goal is to allow transsexual employees to work productively without feeling as if they must hide an essential part of themselves. This includes addressing such issues as transsexual individuals being excluded from employer health care on the basis of their transsexuality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Transgender_Advocacy_Coalition" title="National Transgender Advocacy Coalition">National Transgender Advocacy Coalition</a> is a lobbying organization in the United States dedicated to preserving the civil rights of transsexual individuals. It began in Virginia in 1999 and held its first lobbying event in 2001. It has no paid employees, but consists of a board of experienced lobbyists and activists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Renaissance Education Association</i> is a non-profit organization founded in Pennsylvania that is dedicated to providing education and social support regarding transgender issues. This includes providing educational programs, support groups, and resources to community care providers. It also strives to provide personal and educational resources for individuals struggling with issues related to transsexuality and those close to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Survivor Project</i> is a non-profit organization founded in 1997 that is devoted to assisting intersex and transsexual survivors of domestic and sexual violence. This is done through caring action and education. The Project provides presentations, workshops, and consultation materials to many communities and universities across the United States. It also works to find information regarding the specific issues faced by intersex and transsexual individuals who are victimized. Empowering survivors and allowing them to participate in anti-violence activism is one major philosophy of the organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Transgender Law and Policy Institute (TLPI)</i> was founded by <a href="/wiki/Paisley_Currah" title="Paisley Currah">Paisley Currah</a>, Associate Professor of Political Science at Brooklyn College. It is dedicated to engaging in effective advocacy for transgender people in our society. The TLPI brings experts together to work on law and policy initiatives designed to advance transgender equality. Their website provides information and resources on legislation, case law, employer and college policies and other resources.They also work with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_%26_Lesbian_Advocates_%26_Defenders" title="Gay &amp; Lesbian Advocates &amp; Defenders">Gay &amp; Lesbian Advocates &amp; Defenders</a> (GLAD) in New England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trans*topia is section of Youth Resource (a project of <a href="/wiki/Advocates_for_Youth" title="Advocates for Youth">Advocates for Youth</a>, a nonprofit organization located in Washington D.C.) designed for the needs of transsexual youth. Their website includes articles about being young and transgender, both personal accounts and scientific articles that are intended to help transgender youth become more informed and comfortable with their sexuality and gender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>

The term transgender was coined by John Oliven (1965) and popularized by various transgender people who pioneered the concept and practice of transgenderism. It is sometimes said that Virginia Prince (1976) popularized the term, but history shows that many transgender people advocated the use of this term much more than Prince. The adjective <i>transgendered</i> should not be used [...]. Transsexuals constitute a subset of transgender people."</span></li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2016-07-05</span></span>. <q>Transsexualism is often included within the broader term 'transgender', which is generally considered an umbrella term for people who do not conform to typically accepted gender roles for the sex they were assigned at birth. The term 'transgender' is a word employed by activists to encompass as many groups of gender diverse people as possible. However, many of these groups individually don't identify with the term. Many health clinics and services set up to serve gender variant communities employ the term, however most of the people using these services again don't identify with this term. The rejection of this political category by those that it is designed to cover clearly illustrates the difference between self-identification and categories that are imposed by observers to understand other people.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATranssexual&amp;rft.atitle=Transsexualism&amp;rft.date=2014-03&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gendercentre.org.au%2F&amp;rft.jtitle=Gender+Centre&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-ekins2006-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ekins2006_23-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ekins2006_23-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ekins2006_23-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ekins2006_23-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Ekins, Richard; King, Dave (2006). <i>The Transgender Phenomenon</i>. London: SAGE. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-7619-7164-5" title="Special:BookSources/0-7619-7164-5">0-7619-7164-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATranssexual&amp;rft.aufirst=Richard&amp;rft.au=King%2C+Dave&amp;rft.aulast=Ekins&amp;rft.btitle=The+Transgender+Phenomenon&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=0-7619-7164-5&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pub=SAGE&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Polly-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Polly_24-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Polly_24-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">R Polly, J Nicole, <i>Understanding the transsexual patient: culturally sensitive care in emergency nursing practice</i>, in the <i>Advanced Emergency Nursing Journal</i> (2011): "The use of terminology by transsexual individuals to self-identify varies. As aforementioned, many transsexual individuals prefer the term transgender, or simply trans, as it is more inclusive and carries fewer stigmas. There are some transsexual individuals[,] however, who reject the term transgender; these individuals view transsexualism as a treatable congenital condition. Following medical and/or surgical transition, they live within the binary as either a man or a woman and may not disclose their transition history."</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Swanson-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Swanson_25-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Swanson_25-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">A Swenson, <i>Medical Care of the Transgender Patient</i>, in <i>Family Medicine</i> (2014): "While some transsexual people still prefer to use the term to describe themselves, many transgender people prefer the term transgender to transsexual."</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-Teich-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Teich_65-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Teich, Nicholas (2012). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gdA7AAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA55" rel="nofollow"><i>Transgender 101: A Simple Guide to a Complex Issue</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University_Press" title="Columbia University Press">Columbia University Press</a>. p. 55. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0231504276" title="Special:BookSources/0231504276">0231504276</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 20,</span> 2015</span>. <q>Historically, many transmen who have had phalloplasty have not been satisfied with the results. Doctors continue to make improvements to this surgery, but many surgeons in the United States choose not to perform it because of the high risk of complications (severe scarring or fistulas for example), the significant risk of never regaining sensation in the penis or donor sites, and the chance that the result will not be aesthetically pleasing. However, some transmen are satisfied with their results and would choose to do it again if given the choice.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATranssexual&amp;rft.aufirst=Nicholas&amp;rft.aulast=Teich&amp;rft.btitle=Transgender+101%3A+A+Simple+Guide+to+a+Complex+Issue&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DgdA7AAAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA55&amp;rft.isbn=0231504276&amp;rft.pages=55&amp;rft.pub=Columbia+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-Carroll-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Carroll_67-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Carroll, Janell (2015). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=cy9-BAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PT132" rel="nofollow"><i>Sexuality Now: Embracing Diversity</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>. p. 132. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1305446038" title="Special:BookSources/1305446038">1305446038</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 20,</span> 2015</span>. <q>Penises made from phalloplasty cannot achieve a natural erection, so penile implants of some kind are usually used (we will discuss these implants in more detail in Chapter 14). Overall, metoidioplasty is a simpler procedure than phalloplasty, which explains its popularity. It also has fewer complications, takes less time, and is less expensive (e.g., a metoidioplasty takes about 1 to 2 hours and can cost around $15,000 to 20,000, whereas, a phalloplasty can take about 8 hours can cost more than $65,000).</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATranssexual&amp;rft.aufirst=Janell&amp;rft.aulast=Carroll&amp;rft.btitle=Sexuality+Now%3A+Embracing+Diversity&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dcy9-BAAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPT132&amp;rft.isbn=1305446038&amp;rft.pages=132&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-sept2207-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-sept2207_82-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Landén, M., Wålinder, J., Lundstrom, B. (1996) "...Results: During the 20-year period of the study, 233 requests for sex reassignment were processed, and the incidence data were calculated on the basis of this group. This means that the average annual frequency was 11.6 cases. The number of inhabitants in Sweden over 15 years of age increased during the study period from 6.5 million to 7.1 million, i.e. there was a mean population of 6.8 million (12), which gives an annual incidence of request for sex reassignment of 0.17 per 100,000 inhabitants. The sex ratio (male:female) is 1.4 :1. To resolve the question of whether transsexualism increases or decreases, we divided the group into two 10-year periods. As can be seen from Table 1, not only do our results agree with the Swedish incidence data published in the 1970s, but also they remain remarkably stable over time. Separating from all applications the group with primary transsexualism yielded 188 cases, i.e. 9.4 cases annually. As is shown in Table 2, this corresponds to an incidence of primary transsexualism of 0.14 per 100,000 inhabitants over 15 years of age. It should also be noted that primary transsexualism is equally common in women and men..." in <a class="external text" href="http://www.blackwell-synergy.com/doi/pdf/10.1111/j.1600-0447.1996.tb10645.x" rel="nofollow">Incidence and sex ratio of transsexualism in Sweden</a> from <a class="external text" href="http://www.blackwellpublishing.com/journal.asp?ref=0001-690x" rel="nofollow">Acta Psychiatrica Scandanavica</a>, Volume 93, pages 261-263. Retrieved on 2007-09-22.</span></li>

<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.ftmi.org" rel="nofollow">FTM International</a> – Female To Male International: practical and medical information</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.mtra.org.au/" rel="nofollow">FTM Australia</a> – Comprehensive information for all men identified <i>female</i> at birth in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.ftmguide.org" rel="nofollow">Hudson's FTM Resource Guide</a> – Comprehensive information for female to male trans men and allies – US-based</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.gender.org/about/mission_values.html" rel="nofollow">Gender.org</a> – The home of Gender Education &amp; Advocacy, a nonprofit corporation using the web to provide education and advocacy for transsexual and transgender issues.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.gires.org.uk/Web_Page_Assets/Etiology_definition_signed.htm" rel="nofollow">Definition and Synopsis of the Etiology of Adult Gender Identity Disorder and Transsexualism</a> – prepared by 24 internationally recognized experts, published by the Gender Identity Research and Education Society (GIRES)(See: <a class="external free" href="http://www.gires.org.uk" rel="nofollow">http://www.gires.org.uk</a>)</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.wpath.org/publications_ijt.cfm" rel="nofollow">The International Journal of Transgenderism</a> – The Official Journal of the <a href="/wiki/World_Professional_Association_for_Transgender_Health" title="World Professional Association for Transgender Health">World Professional Association for Transgender Health</a> (formerly HBIGDA). <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20010709083555/http://www.symposion.com/ijt/" rel="nofollow">An archive of IJT Volumes I through V</a> is available, as are <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20010804031026/http://www.symposion.com/ijt/books/index.htm" rel="nofollow">several books on transsexualism</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Harry_Benjamin" title="Harry Benjamin">Harry Benjamin</a>'s "The Transsexual Phenomenon"</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.transparentcy.org/" rel="nofollow">TransParentcy</a> – supports transgender parents and their advocates (lawyers, mental health professionals, friends, family) by providing information and resources.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.tsroadmap.com" rel="nofollow">Transsexual Road Map</a> – consumer information and advice for transsexual women.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.eecs.umich/people/conway/conway.html" rel="nofollow">Lynn Conway's transsexual resources pages</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.annelawrence.com/" rel="nofollow">"Dr. Anne Lawrence On Transsexualism and Sexuality"</a> - detailed information on medical aspects of transition</li>
